Average internet speeds vary wildly from country to country.  </p>\n<p>Which countries have the fastest internet connection? Using data from the <a href=\"https://www.speedtest.net/global-index\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Speedtest Global Index<img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.1.0/72x72/2122.png\" alt=\"™\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /></a>, this map ranks the fastest (and slowest) internet speeds worldwide, comparing both fixed broadband and mobile.</p>\n<h2>What Factors Affect Internet Speed?</h2>\n<p>Before diving in, it’s important to understand the key factors that impact a country’s internet speed. Generally speaking, internet speed depends on:</p>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Infrastructure</strong> or the type of cabling (copper or fiber-optic) that a country’s utilizing to support their internet service. Typically, the newer the infrastructure, the faster the connection.</li>\n<li><strong>Proximity/connection to submarine cables</strong> is important, as these massive <a href=\"https://www.visualcapitalist.com/wired-world-35-years-of-submarine-cables-in-one-map/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">undersea fiber-optic cables</a> transmit about <a href=\"https://thenextweb.com/news/heres-why-cuba-has-painfully-slow-internet-and-what-googles-doing-to-fix-it\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">97%</a> of the world’s communication data. </li>\n<li><strong>The size of a country,</strong> since landmass affects how much it costs to upgrade infrastructure. The smaller the country, the cheaper it is to upgrade cabling. </li>\n<li><strong>Investment</strong>  makes a difference, or how much a country’s government prioritizes internet accessibility.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Of course, other factors may influence a country’s internet speed too, such as government regulation and intentional <a href=\"https://advox.globalvoices.org/2021/06/12/more-internet-security-for-many-not-for-central-asians/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">bandwidth throttling</a>, which is the case in countries like Turkmenistan. </p>\n<h2>Ranked: Fixed Broadband Internet Speeds</h2>\n<p>The Speedtest Global Index uses data from hundreds of millions of people, in more than 190 countries, to measure both fixed broadband and mobile connections. </p>\n<p>When it comes to the fastest fixed broadband, <strong>Singapore</strong> comes in first place, with a download speed of 262.2 mbps—more than double the global average.</p>\n\n<table id=\"tablepress-1856\" class=\"tablepress tablepress-id-1856\">\n<thead>\n<tr class=\"row-1 odd\">\n\t<th class=\"column-1\">#</th><th class=\"column-2\">Country</th><th class=\"column-3\">Global Speed (Mbps)</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody class=\"row-hover\">\n<tr class=\"row-2 even\">\n\t<td class=\"column-1\">1</td><td class=\"column-2\"><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.1.0/72x72/1f1f8-1f1ec.png\" alt=\"🇸🇬\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /> Cuba</td><td class=\"column-3\">3.46</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<!-- #tablepress-1856 from cache -->\n<p>Size could be a factor in Singapore’s speedy internet, as it’s one of the <a href=\"https://www.visualcapitalist.com/worlds-100-smallest-countries/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">smallest</a><br />\n and also densest countries in the world. With a landmass of just 280 square miles, it&#8217;s around the same size as Austin, Texas. </p>\n<p>The country’s government has also prioritized investment in digital infrastructure, especially in recent years. In 2020, the Singaporean government promised to invest <strong>$2.52 billion</strong> towards digital innovation, with a portion dedicated to upgrading the country’s telecom infrastructure.</p>\n<p>At the opposite end of the spectrum, <strong>Cuba</strong> has the slowest fixed broadband, with a speed of 3.46 mbps. Along with poor government funding, Cuba also has limited access to submarine cables. While most countries are connected to several, Cuba is only connected to <strong>one.</strong> </p>\n<h2>Ranked: Mobile Internet Speeds</h2>\n<p>Mobile internet uses cell towers to wirelessly transmit internet to your phone. Not only is mobile data fast in the UAE, it’s also relatively cheap, compared to other countries on the ranking. The average cost of 1 GB of data in the UAE is around <a href=\"https://www.visualcapitalist.com/cost-of-mobile-data-worldwide/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">$3.78</a>, while in South Korea (#2 on the list) it’s $10.94.</p>\n<h2>The Future is 5G</h2>\n<p>Innovation and new technologies are changing the digital landscape, and things like <a href=\"https://www.visualcapitalist.com/visualizing-the-state-of-5g-networks-worldwide/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">5G networks</a> are becoming more mainstream across the globe. </p>\n<p>Because of the rapidly changing nature of this industry, the data behind this ranking is updated monthly to provide the latest look at internet speeds across the globe. </p>\n<p>This means the bar is gradually raising when it comes to internet speed, as faster, stronger internet connections become the norm. And countries that aren’t equipped to handle these souped-up networks will lag behind even further. </p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\"
